25:T2d51,<entryFree id="n35367" key="قَرَأَ الشَّىْءَ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">قَرَأَ الشَّىْءَ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, [aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">قَرَاَ</orth>
                  </form>,] inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">قُرْآنٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He collected together the thing; put it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">drew it, together;</hi> (S, O, K, TA;) <hi rend="ital">part to part,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">portion to portion.</hi> (S, O, TA.) [This seems to be generally regarded as the primary signification.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Hence the saying of the Arabs, <foreign lang="ar">مَا قَرَأَتْ هٰذِهِ النَّاقَةُ سَلًى قَطُّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَا قَرَأَتْ جِنِينًا</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">This she-camel has not contracted her womb upon a young one:</hi> (S, O, TA:) but most say that the meaning is, <hi rend="ital">her womb has not comprised,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">enclosed, a fœtus:</hi> or the former saying means <hi rend="ital">she has not borne a fœtus:</hi> accord. to AHeyth, this same saying and <foreign lang="ar">مَا قَرَأَتْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مَلْقُوحًا</foreign> are both said to mean, by some, <hi rend="ital">she has not borne in her womb a young one ever:</hi> and by some, <hi rend="ital">she has not let fall a young one, ever;</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">she has not been pregnant:</hi> and accord. to ISh, one says,   
      <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ الفَحْلُ النَّاقَةَ عَلَى غَيْرِ <ref cref="n35367-1" target="قَرْءٍ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [which seems to mean <hi rend="ital">The stallion covered the she-camel without her bringing forth,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">becoming pregnant;</hi> for he adds that <foreign lang="ar">قرء الناقة</foreign> means <foreign lang="ar">ضعتها</foreign>; app. <foreign lang="ar">ضَعَتُهَا</foreign> or <foreign lang="ar">ضِعَتُهَا</foreign>; but I have not found <foreign lang="ar">ضَعَةٌ</foreign> nor <foreign lang="ar">ضِعَةٌ</foreign> among the inf. ns. of <foreign lang="ar">وَضَعَتْ</foreign> meaning “ she brought forth; ” and I rather think that the right reading is <foreign lang="ar">ضَغَنُهَا</foreign> or <foreign lang="ar">ضِغْنُهَا</foreign>, and that the meaning therefore is, <hi rend="ital">without her inclining,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">being desirous:</hi> see 10, third sentence; and see <foreign lang="ar">قَرْءُ الفَرَسِ</foreign>]: and there is another saying; that <foreign lang="ar">لَمْ تَقْرَأْ جَنِينًا</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">She has not,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">did not, cast forth a fœtus,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a young one.</hi> (TA.) One says also, of the she-camel, (K, TA,) and of the ewe, or she-goat, (TA,) <foreign lang="ar">قَرَأَتْ</foreign>, alone, meaning <hi rend="ital">She became pregnant:</hi> (K, TA:) and likewise, of the pregnant [in general], or of the she-camel, accord. to different copies of the K, (TA,) meaning <hi rend="ital">she brought forth:</hi> (K, TA:) ISh says that <foreign lang="ar">قَرَأَتْ</foreign> is used in relation to a she-camel; and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n35367-2" target="أَقْرَأَتْ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, in relation to a woman: [each, app., in the former sense and in the latter:] and that one says   
      <foreign lang="ar">نَاقَةٌ <ref cref="n35367-3" target="قَارِئٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n35381"/></foreign>; pl. <foreign lang="ar">نُوقٌ قَوَارِئُ</foreign>. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  See also 4.       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">قَرَأَ الكِتَابِ</foreign>, (S, O, Msb, * K, *) and <foreign lang="ar">بِهِ</foreign>, (Msb, * K,) the verb being trans. by itself and by means of <foreign lang="ar">ب</foreign>, or this particle is redundant, (Msb,) and sometimes the <foreign lang="ar">ء</foreign> is suppressed, so that one says [<foreign lang="ar">قَرَى</foreign> and] <foreign lang="ar">قَرَيْتُ</foreign> &amp;c., (TA,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">قَرَاَ</orth>
                  </form> and      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">قَرُاَ</orth>
                  </form>, (K,) the latter aor. on the authority of Ez-Zejjájee, as is said in the L, but generally ignored, (TA,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">قِرَآءَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">قُرْآنٌ</foreign> (S, O, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">قَرْءٌ</foreign>, (Msb, K,) this last mentioned by Az; (Msb;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n35367-4" target="اقترأهُ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (K;) <hi rend="ital">He read</hi> [<hi rend="ital">the book,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">Scripture</hi>], or <hi rend="ital">recited</hi> [<hi rend="ital">it</hi>]: (K, TA:) or <foreign lang="ar">قَرَأْتُ القُرْآنَ</foreign> means [properly, or etymologically, accord. to some,] <hi rend="ital">I uttered</hi> [<hi rend="ital">the words of</hi>] <hi rend="ital">the Kur-án in a state of combination</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">uninterruptedly</hi>]; (O, TA;) as Ktr is related to have said: (O:) [or <foreign lang="ar">قَرَأَ</foreign> as used in a case of this kind app. signifies properly <hi rend="ital">he read,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">recited,</hi> the Scripture <hi rend="ital">chanting;</hi> like as <foreign lang="ar">أَنْشَدَ</foreign> properly signifies “ he recited ” poetry “ chanting with a high voice: ” (for Scripture and poetry are usually chanted:) then, <hi rend="ital">he read,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">recited,</hi> anything <hi rend="ital">in any manner,</hi> without, or from, or in, a book.] It is said in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ أَرَادَ أَنْ يَقْرَأَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">القُرْآنَ غَضًّا كَمَا أُنْزِلَ فَلْيَقْرَأْهُ قِرَآءَةَ أُمِّ عَبْدٍ</foreign> [He who desires to read, or recite, <hi rend="ital">the Kur-án freshly, like as it was revealed, let him read,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">recite, it in the manner of Ibn-Umm-'Abd</hi>]; meaning <foreign lang="ar">فَلْيُرَنِّلْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كَتَرْتِيلِهِ</foreign> [properly, <hi rend="ital">let him read,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">recite, in a leisurely manner, with distinct utterance, and with moderation;</hi> but conventionally, <hi rend="ital">let him chant, in a peculiar, distinct, and leisurely, manner; like as he did</hi>]: or <foreign lang="ar">يُحَزِّنْ كَتَحْزِينِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">let him read,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">recite, with a slender and plaintive voice, like as he did</hi>]: or <foreign lang="ar">يَحْدُرْهُ كَحَدْرِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">let him read it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">recite it, quickly, like as he did</hi>]. (O.) And in a trad. of I'Ab, it is said, <foreign lang="ar">كَانَ لَا يَقْرَأُ فِى الظُّهْرِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَالعَصْرِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">He used not to recite</hi> [the Kur- án] <hi rend="ital">aloud in the</hi> [prayers of the] <hi rend="ital">noon and the</hi> [period of the afternoon called the] <foreign lang="ar">عْصر</foreign>: or <hi rend="ital">he used not to make himself to hear his reciting:</hi> as though he heard persons reciting and making themselves and those near them to hear. (TA.) The saying, in the Kur [lxxv. 17 and 18], <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْنَا جَمْعَهُ وَقُرْآنَهُ فَإِذَا قَرَأْنَاهُ فَٱتَّبِع قُرْآنَهُ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">Verily on us is the collecting thereof</hi> [i. e. of the Kur-án] <hi rend="ital">and the reciting thereof; and when we recite it, then follow thou the reciting thereof:</hi> or, accord. to I'Ab, <hi rend="ital">and when we explain it to thee, then do thou according to that which we have explained to thee:</hi> (S, O, TA:) or the meaning [signified and implied] is, <hi rend="ital">verily on us is the collecting thereof</hi> in thy mind, <hi rend="ital">and the fixing the recitation thereof on thy tongue; and when we recite it</hi> to thee by the tongue of Gabriel, <hi rend="ital">then follow thou the reciting thereof,</hi> and often recur therein so that it may become firmly rooted in thy understanding: (Bd:) [therefore <foreign lang="ar">قُرْآنَهُ</foreign> in the former instance means <hi rend="ital">the teaching</hi> thee <hi rend="ital">to recite it;</hi> and thus we may explain the assertion that] <foreign lang="ar">قَرَأَ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n35367-5" target="أَقْرَأَ" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> are syn. in like manner as are <foreign lang="ar">عَلَا قِرْنَهُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">استعلاهُ</foreign>. (Sb, TA.)                      <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> The <foreign lang="ar">وَبَآء</foreign> [by which is here meant the <hi rend="ital">common,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">general, disease</hi>] (As, S, O, K) of a country; (S, O;) of which it is said that when a person has come to that country and remained in it fifteen nights [or days, accord. to one of my copies of the S,] the <foreign lang="ar">قرأة</foreign> thereof quits him; or, as the people of El-Hijáz say, its <foreign lang="ar">قِرَة</foreign>; meaning that if he be affected with a malady after that, it will not be from the <foreign lang="ar">وبآء</foreign> [or <foreign lang="ar">قرأة</foreign>] of the country: (As, S, O;) and it is also termed   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n35376-1" target="قِرْءٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n35375"/></foreign>. (TA. [But I think it not improbable that this last word may have originated in a mistranscription of <foreign lang="ar">قِرَةٌ</foreign>.])       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  See also 4, second sentence.    </entryFree>2c:Td45,<entryFree id="n35377" key="القُرْآنُ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">القُرْآنُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> is said by some of the erudite to be originally an inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">قَرَأْتُ الشَّىْءَ</foreign> meaning “ I collected together the thing, ” or of <foreign lang="ar">قَرَأْتُ الكِتَابَ</foreign> meaning “ I read, or recited, the book, or Scripture; ” and then conventionally applied to signify <hi rend="ital">The Book of God that was revealed to Mo- hammad:</hi> (Kull:) it is [also expl. as signifying] <hi rend="ital">the revelation,</hi> (K, TA,) meaning <hi rend="ital">that which is termed</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">العَزِيز</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">the mighty,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">inimitable,</hi> &amp;c.], <hi rend="ital">which is read,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">recited, and written in books,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">volumes:</hi> (TA:) used as a subst., and unrestrictedly, it is applied in the language of the law to <hi rend="ital">the substance itself</hi> [<hi rend="ital">whereof the Kur-án consists</hi>], and lexically to <hi rend="ital">the alphabetical letters</hi> [<hi rend="ital">in which it is written</hi>] for these are what are read; as when one says, <foreign lang="ar">كَتَبْتُ القُرْآنَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I wrote the Kur-án</hi>], and <foreign lang="ar">مَسِسْتُهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I touched it</hi>]: (Msb:) [and without the article <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign>, it is applied to <hi rend="ital">any portion of the Kur-án:</hi>] accord. to AO, (S,) and Zj, (TA,) it is thus called because it collects and comprises the <foreign lang="ar">سُوَر</foreign> [or chapters]: (S, O, TA:) and IAth says that the original meaning of the word is <hi rend="ital">the collection;</hi> and that the <foreign lang="ar">قُرْآن</foreign> is so called because it has collected the histories [of the prophets &amp;c.], and commands and prohibitions, and promises and threats, [and the like is said in the O,] and the <foreign lang="ar">آيَات</foreign> [i. e. verses, or signs], and the <foreign lang="ar">سُوَر</foreign> [or chapters]: but Ismá'eel Ibn-Kustan- teen, to whom, as a disciple to his preceptor, EshSháfi'ee read, or recited, the Kur-án, is related on the latter's authority to have said that <foreign lang="ar">القُرَانُ</foreign> is a subst., and with hemz, and not taken from <foreign lang="ar">قَرَأْتُ</foreign>, but is a name for <hi rend="ital">the Book of God,</hi> like <foreign lang="ar">التَّوْرَاةُ</foreign> [the Book of the Law revealed to Moses] and <foreign lang="ar">الإِنْجِيلُ</foreign> [the Gospel]: and it is related that Aboo-'Amr Ibn-El-'Alà used to pronounce <foreign lang="ar">القران</foreign> without hemz [like many others, but it is, and always has been, pronounced by most with hemz]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  It is also applied to <hi rend="ital">The divinely appointed act of prayer</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">الصَّلَاةُ</foreign>) because it comprises recitation [of words of the Kur-án]. (IAth, TA.)    </entryFree>2d:T5c7,<entryFree id="n35380" key="قُرَّآءٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">قُرَّآءٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, O, K,) an epithet applied to a man and to a woman, (Fr, TA,) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n35380-1" target="قَارِئٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n35381"/></foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n35380-2" target="مُتَقَرِّئٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, (K,) <hi rend="ital">A devotee;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">one who devotes himself</hi> [and in the case of the first of these epithets <hi rend="ital">herself</hi>] <hi rend="ital">to religious exercises</hi> [and particularly <hi rend="ital">to the reading,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">reciting, of the Kur-án</hi>]: (S, O, K:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">قُرَّاؤُونَ</foreign> (S, K) and <foreign lang="ar">قَرَارِىْءُ</foreign>, (K, TA,) [in the CK <foreign lang="ar">قَرارِئُ</foreign> and] in a MS copy of the K <foreign lang="ar">قَوَارِئُ</foreign>, which might be a pl. of <foreign lang="ar">قَارِئٌ</foreign>; and in the L <foreign lang="ar">قَرَائِئُ</foreign>.                   <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">قَارِئٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
